<p style='margin:0cm;font-size:16px;font-family:"Liberation Serif",serif;margin-top:2.5pt;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:6.25pt;margin-left:12.5pt;'><span style='font-size:12px;font-family:"Helvetica",sans-serif;color:black;'>Another way of explaining the same thing because engineers typically are very smart, engineers are very quick at thinking and engineers love solving problems. So if you&apos;re not giving them enough information they will solve the wrong problem. Was it a robin&apos;s red breast and a snowy scene? Was it a fire engine? You&apos;re probably going to know which of those three things it was if you had four more pieces from the jigsaw box without knowing the big picture. So try to inject a few more bits of context with your questions. Try to encourage your tech team to always ask three questions of you or of the product owner or whoever it is to help them validate they&apos;ve understood it.
